# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repositories (version-pinned mirrors):**

- `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

**Sourcegraph Repositories:** `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, `github.com/sg-evals/api--v0.32.0`

# Kubernetes Controller Runtime Reconciler Registration

## Your Task

Trace how a controller registers itself with the controller-runtime Manager in kubernetes/kubernetes. Find the Go source files that define the Reconciler interface, implement SetupWithManager, and wire the controller into the manager's reconcile loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Core Reconciler Interface\n\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). Perfect! I've successfully created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive findings on how controllers register themselves with the controller-runtime Manager in Kubernetes. Here's a summary of what I've documented:

## Summary

**Key Findings:**

1. **Reconciler Interface** - The core abstraction defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go`:
   - Single method: `Reconcile(context.Context, Request) (Result, error)`
   - Controllers implement this to define their business logic

2. **Builder Pattern** - Controllers wire themselves via `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`:
   - `ControllerManagedBy(manager)` - Binds controller to a Manager
   - `.For()`, `.Owns()`, `.Watches()` - Configure watch sources
   - `.Complete(reconciler)` or `.Build()` - Finalizes setup

3. **SetupWithManager Pattern** - Standard implementation pattern:
   ```go
   func (r *Reconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {
       return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).
           For(&MyResource{}).
           Owns(&Pod{}).
           Complete(r)
   }
   ```

4. **Kubernetes Integration** - The Kubernetes kube-controller-manager uses its own pattern:
   - `ControllerDescriptor` with `InitFunc` callbacks
   - Base `Interface` with `Name()` method
   - Different but complementary to controller-runtime pattern

5. **Reconciliation Loop** - Orchestrated by Manager:
   - Event sources trigger enqueuing
   - Manager calls `Reconciler.Reconcile()` with Request
   - Result determines requeue behavior

The answer file contains 7 relevant files, 10 key symbols, a 10-step call chain, and detailed narrative explanation covering all aspects of the controller registration mechanism.

changes to systems external to the cluster (e.g. cloudproviders, github, etc).\n58: \n59: reconcile implementations compare the state specified in an object by a user against the actual cluster state,\n60: and then perform operations to make the actual cluster state reflect the state specified by the user.\n61: \n62: Typically, reconcile is triggered by a Controller in response to cluster Events (e.g. Creating, Updating,\n63: Deleting Kubernetes objects) or external Events (GitHub Webhooks, polling external sources, etc).\n64: \n65: Example reconcile Logic:\n66: \n67: * Read an object and all the Pods it owns.\n68: * Observe that the object spec specifies 5 replicas but actual cluster contains only 1 Pod replica.\n69: * Create 4 Pods and set their OwnerReferences to the object.\n70: \n71: reconcile may be implemented as either a type:\n72: \n73: \ttype reconciler struct {}\n74: \n75: \tfunc (reconciler) Reconcile(ctx context.Context, o reconcile.Request) nil\n85: \t})\n86: \n87: Reconciliation is level-based, meaning action isn't driven off changes in individual Events, but instead is\n88: driven by actual cluster state read from the apiserver or a local cache.\n89: For example if responding to a Pod Delete Event, the Request won't contain that a Pod was deleted,\n90: instead the reconcile function observes this when reading the cluster state interface through the Builder pattern to the Manager.\\n\\n### 1. Core Reconciler Interface\\n\\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). This interface defines:\\n\\n```go\\ntype Reconciler interface {\\n    Reconcile(context.Context, Request) (Result, error)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe Reconciler interface is implemented by any controller that wants to reconcile Kubernetes resources. The Request contains the NamespacedName of the object being reconciled, and Result specifies whether the reconcile should be requeued.\\n\\n### 2. Builder Pattern for Controller Setup\\n\\nControllers implement the **SetupWithManager** pattern by using the Builder from `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`. The Builder provides a fluent API for wiring up a controller:\\n\\n**Key functions:**\\n- `ControllerManagedBy(m manager.Manager) *Builder` - Creates a new controller builder bound to a Manager\\n- `Builder.For(object client.Object) *Builder` - Specifies the primary resource type to reconcile\\n- `Builder.Owns(object client.Object) *Builder` - Registers owned resource types for watch\\n- `Builder.Watches(object client.Object, handler) *Builder` - Adds custom watch sources\\n- `Builder.Complete(r reconcile.Reconciler) error` - Finalizes the controller setup\\n- `Builder.Build(r reconcile.Reconciler) (controller.Controller, error)` - Builds and returns the controller\\n\\n### 3. Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Controller Creation\\n\\nThe `doController()` method in Builder creates the actual Controller by:\\n- Calling `newController` (which is `controller.New`)\\n- Passing the Reconciler, Manager, and controller options\\n- The Controller implements the internal `controller.Controller` interface defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/controller/controller.go`\\n\\n### Key Architectural Points\\n\\n- **Decoupling**: Controllers implement only the Reconciler interface; the Builder and Manager handle all event watching and queueing\\n- **Level-Based**: Reconciliation is level-based (not edge-based), meaning the reconciler observes actual state and doesn't rely on event details\\n- **Composability**: Multiple controllers can be registered with the same Manager, each managing different resource types\\n- **Error Handling**: Non-nil errors trigger exponential backoff requeue; TerminalError bypasses requeue\\n\\nThis architecture enables clean separation of concerns: controllers focus on business logic (implementing Reconcile), while the framework handles watching, queueing, and lifecycle management.\"\n}\n",

controller-runtime Manager\\n\\nControllers in the Kubernetes ecosystem using controller-runtime register themselves with a Manager through a well-defined pattern that traces from the Reconciler interface through the Builder pattern to the Manager.\\n\\n### 1. Core Reconciler Interface\\n\\nThe foundation of controller registration is the **Reconciler interface** defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/reconcile/reconcile.go` (available in github.com/sg-evals/cilium--v1.16.5). This interface defines:\\n\\n```go\\ntype Reconciler interface {\\n    Reconcile(context.Context, Request) (Result, error)\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe Reconciler interface is implemented by any controller that wants to reconcile Kubernetes resources. The Request contains the NamespacedName of the object being reconciled, and Result specifies whether the reconcile should be requeued.\\n\\n### 2. Builder Pattern for Controller Setup\\n\\nControllers implement the **SetupWithManager** pattern by using the Builder from `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`. The Builder provides a fluent API for wiring up a controller:\\n\\n**Key functions:**\\n- `ControllerManagedBy(m manager.Manager) *Builder` - Creates a new controller builder bound to a Manager\\n- `Builder.For(object client.Object) *Builder` - Specifies the primary resource type to reconcile\\n- `Builder.Owns(object client.Object) *Builder` - Registers owned resource types for watch\\n- `Builder.Watches(object client.Object, handler) *Builder` - Adds custom watch sources\\n- `Builder.Complete(r reconcile.Reconciler) error` - Finalizes the controller setup\\n- `Builder.Build(r reconcile.Reconciler) (controller.Controller, error)` - Builds and returns the controller\\n\\n### 3. Implementation Pattern\\n\\nControllers typically implement SetupWithManager like this (example from Cilium in vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime):\\n\\n```go\\nfunc (r *MyReconciler) SetupWithManager(mgr ctrl.Manager) error {\\n    return ctrl.NewControllerManagedBy(mgr).\\n        For(&myv1.MyResource{}).\\n        Owns(&corev1.Pod{}).\\n        Complete(r)\\n}\\n```\\n\\n### 4. Kubernetes Controller Manager Integration\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0`, controllers use a different internal pattern but still follow the same principles:\\n\\n- **ControllerDescriptor** in `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` wraps controller metadata\\n- **InitFunc** is the function type that creates and starts a controller, returning `controller.Interface`\\n- Controller **Interface** is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go` with a `Name()` method\\n\\n### 5. Reconciliation Loop Mechanism\\n\\nThe Manager orchestrates the reconciliation loop:\\n\\n1. **Event Sources**: The builder configures watch sources via `doWatch()` in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/builder/controller.go`\\n2. **Event Handling**: When resources change, events are enqueued\\n3. **Reconciliation**: The Manager's internal Controller calls `Reconciler.Reconcile()` with the enqueued Request\\n4. **Requeue Logic**: Based on the Result, the Manager decides whether to requeue immediately, after a duration, or complete\\n\\n### 6. Watch Configuration\\n\\nThe Builder's `doWatch()` method (lines 275-338 in controller.go):\\n- Registers watchers for primary resources via `For()`\\n- Registers watchers for owned resources via `Owns()` using `EnqueueRequestForOwner`\\n- Sets up additional watches via `Watches()` with custom handlers\\n- Validates that at least one watch is configured\\n\\n### 7. Controller Creation\\n\\nThe `doController()` method in Builder creates the actual Controller by:\\n- Calling `newController` (which is `controller.New`)\\n- Passing the Reconciler, Manager, and controller options\\n- The Controller implements the internal `controller.Controller` interface defined in `vendor/sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime/pkg/controller/controller.go`\\n\\n### Key Architectural Points\\n\\n- **Decoupling**: Controllers implement only the Reconciler interface; the Builder and Manager handle all event watching and queueing\\n- **Level-Based**: Reconciliation is level-based (not edge-based), meaning the reconciler observes actual state and doesn't rely on event details\\n- **Composability**: Multiple controllers can be registered with the same Manager, each managing different resource types\\n- **Error Handling**: Non-nil errors trigger exponential backoff requeue; TerminalError bypasses requeue\\n\\nThis architecture enables clean separation of concerns: controllers focus on business logic (implementing Reconcile), while the framework handles watching, queueing, and lifecycle management.\"\n}\n",
